Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-702(2)(b): it is dismissed or results in findings favorable to the educator.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-702(3): (2) An educator who recovers under this section is also entitled to recover reasonable attorneys' fees and costs necessarily incurred by the educator in recovering the attorneys' fees and costs allowed under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-703 Professional competence or performance -- Administrative hearing by local school board -- Action on complaint.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-703(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-703(1)(a): No civil action by or on behalf of a student relating to the professional competence or performance of a licensed employee of a school district, or to the discipline of students by a licensed employee, application of in loco parentis, or a violation of ethical conduct by an employee of a school district, may be brought in a court until at least 60 days after the filing of a written complaint with the local school board of the district, or until findings have been issued by the local school board after a hearing on the complaint, whichever is sooner.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-703(1)(b): (1)(a) As used in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-703(1)(c): A parent of a student has standing to file a civil action against an employee who provides services to a school attended by the student.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-703(2): (1) Within 15 days of receiving a complaint under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-703(3): If a complaint is referred to the state board, no civil action may be brought in a court on matters relating to the complaint until the state board has provided a hearing and issued its findings or until 90 days after the filing of the complaint with the local school board, whichever is sooner.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-801 Mediation of contract negotiations.
-------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-801(1): The president of a professional local organization which represents a majority of the licensed employees of a school district or the chairman or president of a local school board may, after negotiating for 90 days, declare an impasse by written notification to the other party and to the state board.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-801(2): The party declaring the impasse may request the state superintendent to appoint a mediator for the purpose of helping to resolve the impasse if the parties to the dispute have not been able to agree on a third party mediator.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-801(3): Within five working days after receipt of the written request, the state superintendent shall appoint a mediator who is mutually acceptable to the local school board and the professional organization representing a majority of the licensed employees.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-801(4): The mediator shall meet with the parties, either jointly or separately, and attempt to settle the impasse.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-801(5): The mediator may not, without the consent of both parties, make findings of fact or recommend terms for settlement.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-801(6): Both parties shall equally share the costs of mediation.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-801(7): Nothing in this section prevents the parties from adopting a written mediation procedure other than that provided in this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-801(8): If the parties have a mediation procedure, they shall follow that procedure.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-802 Appointment of hearing officer -- Hearing process.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-802(1): 53E-6-801 If a mediator appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-802(2): Within five working days after receipt of the request, the state superintendent shall appoint a hearing officer who is mutually acceptable to the local school board and the professional organization representing a majority of the certificated employees.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-802(3): The hearing officer may not, without consent of both parties, be the same person who served as mediator.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-802(4): The hearing officer shall meet with the parties, either jointly or separately, may make inquiries and investigations, and may issue subpoenas for the production of persons or documents relevant to all issues in dispute.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-802(5): The state board and departments, divisions, authorities, bureaus, agencies, and officers of the  state, local school boards, and the professional organization shall furnish the hearing officer, on request, all relevant records, documents, and information in their possession.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-802(6): If the final positions of the parties are not resolved before the hearing ends, the hearing officer shall prepare a written report containing the agreements of the parties with respect to all resolved negotiated contract issues and the positions that the hearing officer considers appropriate on all unresolved final positions of the parties.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-802(7): The hearing officer shall submit the report to the parties privately within 10 working days after the conclusion of the hearing or within the date established for the submission of posthearing briefs, but not later than 20 working days after the hearing officer's appointment.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-802(8): Either the hearing officer, the professional organization, or the local school board may make the report public if the dispute is not settled within 10 working days after its receipt from the hearing officer.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-802(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-802(9)(a): The state superintendent may determine the majority status of any professional organization which requests assistance under this section.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-802(9)(b): The decision of the state superintendent is final unless it is clearly inconsistent with the evidence.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-901 Substitute teachers.
----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-901(1): A substitute teacher need not hold a license to teach, but school districts are encouraged to hire licensed personnel as substitutes when available.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-901(2): 53G-11-402 A person must submit to a background check under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-901(3): A teacher's position in the classroom may not be filled by an unlicensed substitute teacher for more than a total of 20 days during any school year unless licensed personnel are not available.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-901(4): A person who is ineligible to hold a license for any reason other than professional preparation may not serve as a substitute teacher.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-902 Teacher leaders.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-902(1): As used in this section, "teacher" means an educator who has an assignment to teach in a classroom.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-902(2): There is created the role of a teacher leader to:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-902(2)(a): work with a student teacher and a teacher who supervises a student teacher;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-902(2)(b): assist with the training of a recently hired teacher; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-902(2)(c): support school-based professional learning.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-902(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (2) In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-902(3)(a): (2) define the role of a teacher leader, including the functions described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-902(3)(b): establish the minimum criteria for a teacher to qualify as a teacher leader.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-902(4): The state board shall solicit recommendations from school districts and educators regarding:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-902(4)(a): appropriate resources to provide a teacher leader; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-902(4)(b): appropriate ways to compensate a teacher leader.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-903 STEM education endorsements and incentive program.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-903(1): As used in this section, "STEM" means science, technology, engineering, and mathematics.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-903(2): (2)(a) The state board shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-903(2)(a): develop STEM education endorsements; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-903(2)(b): (2)(a) create and implement financial incentives for:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-903(2)(b)(i): (2)(a) an educator to earn an elementary or secondary STEM education endorsement described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-903(2)(b)(ii): a school district or a charter school to have STEM endorsed educators on staff.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-903(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; (2) In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-903(3)(a): an incentive for an educator to take a course leading to a STEM education endorsement may only be given for a course that carries higher-education credit; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-903(3)(b): a school district or a charter school may consider a STEM education endorsement as part of an educator's salary schedule.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1100 Article I -- Purpose.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1100(1): The purpose of this compact is to facilitate the mobility of teachers across the member states, with the goal of supporting teachers through a new pathway to licensure. Through this compact, the member states seek to establish a collective regulatory framework that expedites and enhances the ability of teachers to move across state lines.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1100(2): This compact is intended to achieve the following objectives and should be interpreted accordingly. The member states hereby ratify the same intentions by subscribing hereto:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1100(2)(a): create a streamlined pathway to licensure mobility for teachers;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1100(2)(b): support the relocation of eligible military spouses;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1100(2)(c): facilitate and enhance the exchange of licensure, investigative, and disciplinary information between the member states;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1100(2)(d): enhance the power of state and district level education officials to hire qualified, competent teachers by removing barriers to the employment of out-of-state teachers;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1100(2)(e): support the retention of teachers in the profession by removing barriers to relicensure in a new state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1100(2)(f): maintain state sovereignty in the regulation of the teaching profession.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101 Article II -- Definitions.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1): 53E-6-1107; Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act As used in this compact, and except as otherwise provided, the following definitions shall govern the terms herein:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(a): "Active military member" means any person with full-time duty status in the armed forces of the United States, including members of the National Guard and Reserve;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(b): "Adverse action" means any limitation or restriction imposed by a member state's licensing authority, such as revocation, suspension, reprimand, probation, or limitation on the licensee's ability to work as a teacher;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(c): "Bylaws" means those bylaws established by the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(d): "Career and technical education license" means a current, valid authorization issued by a member state's licensing authority allowing an individual to serve as a teacher in P-12 public educational settings in a specific career and technical education area;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(e): "Charter member states" means a member state that has enacted legislation to adopt this compact where such legislation predates the initial meeting of the commission after the effective date of the compact;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(f): "Commission" means the interstate administrative body which membership consists of delegates of all states that have enacted this compact, and which is known as the Interstate Teacher Mobility Compact Commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(g): "Commissioner" means the delegate of a member state;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(h): "Eligible license" means a license to engage in the teaching profession which requires at least a bachelor's degree and the completion of a state approved program for teacher licensure;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(i): "Eligible military spouse" means the spouse of an individual in full-time duty status in the active armed forces of the United States including members of the National Guard and Reserve moving as a result of a military mission or military career progression requirements or are on their terminal move as a result of separation or retirement, to include surviving spouses of deceased military members;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(j): "Executive committee" means a group of commissioners elected or appointed to act on behalf of, and within the powers granted to them by, the commission as provided for herein;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(k): "Licensing authority" means an official, agency, board, or other entity of a state that is responsible for the licensing and regulation of teachers authorized to teach in P-12 public educational settings;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(l): "Member state" means any state that has adopted this compact, including all agencies and officials of such a state;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(m): "Receiving state" means any state where a teacher has applied for licensure under this compact;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(n): 53E-6-1107; Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act "Rule" means any regulation promulgated by the commission in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(o): "State" means a state, territory, or possession of the United States, and the District of Columbia;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(p): "State practice laws" means a member state's laws, rules, and regulations that govern the teaching profession, define the scope of such profession, and create the methods and grounds for imposing discipline;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(q): "State specific requirements" means a requirement for licensure covered in coursework or examination that include content of unique interest to the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(r): "Teacher" means an individual who currently holds an authorization from a member state that forms the basis for employment in the P-12 public schools of the state to provide instruction in a specific subject area, grade level, or student population; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(1)(s): "Unencumbered license" means a current, valid authorization issued by a member state's licensing authority allowing an individual to serve as a teacher in P-12 public educational settings. An unencumbered license is not a restricted, probationary, provisional, substitute, or temporary credential.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1101(2): 53E-1-102 The definitions described in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1102 Article III -- Licensure under the compact.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1102(1): Licensure under this compact pertains only to the initial grant of a license by the receiving state. Nothing herein applies to any subsequent or ongoing compliance requirements that a receiving state might require for teachers.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1102(2): Each member state shall, in accordance with the rules of the commission, define, compile, and update as necessary, a list of eligible licenses and career and technical educational licenses that the member state is willing to consider for equivalency under this compact and provide the list to the commission. The list shall include those licenses that a receiving state is willing to grant to teachers from other member states, pending a determination of equivalency by the receiving state's licensing authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1102(3): Upon the receipt of an application for licensure by a teacher holding an unencumbered eligible license, the receiving state shall determine which of the receiving state's eligible licenses the teacher is qualified to hold and shall grant such a license or licenses to the applicant. Such a determination shall be made in the sole discretion of the receiving state's licensing authority and may include a determination that the applicant is not eligible for any of the receiving state's eligible licenses. For all teachers who hold an unencumbered license, the receiving state shall grant one or more unencumbered license(s) that, in the receiving state's sole discretion, are equivalent to the license(s) held by the teacher in any other member state.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1102(4): For active military members and eligible military spouses who hold a license that is not unencumbered, the receiving state shall grant an equivalent license or licenses that, in the receiving state's sole discretion, is equivalent to the license or licenses held by the teacher in any other member state, except where the receiving state does not have an equivalent license.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1102(5): For a teacher holding an unencumbered career and technical education license, the receiving state shall grant an unencumbered license equivalent to the career and technical education license held by the applying teacher and issued by another member state, as determined by the receiving state in its sole discretion, except where a career and technical education teacher does not hold a bachelor's degree and the receiving state requires a bachelor's degree for licenses to teach career and technical education. A receiving state may require career and technical education teachers to meet state industry recognized requirements, if required by law in the receiving state.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1103 Article IV -- Licensure not under the compact.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1103(1): 53E-6-1105 Except as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1103(2): When a teacher is required to renew a license received pursuant to this compact, the state granting such a license may require the teacher to complete state specific requirements as a condition of licensure renewal or advancement in that state.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1103(3): For the purposes of determining compensation, a receiving state may require additional information from teachers receiving a license under the provisions of this compact.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1103(4): Nothing in this compact shall be construed to limit the power of a member state to control and maintain ownership of its information pertaining to teachers, or limit the application of a member state's laws or regulations governing the ownership, use, or dissemination of information pertaining to teachers.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1103(5): Nothing in this compact shall be construed to invalidate or alter any existing agreement or other cooperative arrangement which a member state may already be a party to, or limit the ability of a member state to participate in any future agreement or other cooperative arrangement to:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1103(5)(a): award teaching licenses or other benefits based on additional professional credentials, including, but not limited to National Board Certification;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1103(5)(b): participate in the exchange of names of teachers whose license has been subject to an adverse action by a member state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1103(5)(c): participate in any agreement or cooperative arrangement with a nonmember state.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1104 Article V -- Teacher qualifications and requirements for licensure under the compact.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1104(1): 53E-6-1102(4) Except as provided for active military members or eligible military spouses in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1104(2): A teacher eligible to receive a license under this compact shall, unless otherwise provided for herein:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1104(2)(a): upon their application to receive a license under this compact, undergo a criminal background check in the receiving state in accordance with the laws and regulations of the receiving state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1104(2)(b): provide the receiving state with the information in addition to the information required for licensure for the purposes of determining compensation, if applicable.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1105 Article VI -- Discipline and adverse actions.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1105(1): Nothing in this Compact shall be deemed or construed to limit the authority of a member state to investigate or impose disciplinary measures on teachers according to the state practice laws thereof.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1105(2): Member states shall be authorized to receive, and shall provide, files and information regarding the investigation and discipline, if any, of teachers in other member states upon request. Any member state receiving such information or files shall protect and maintain the security and confidentiality thereof, in at least the same manner that it maintains its own investigatory or disciplinary files and information. Prior to disclosing any disciplinary or investigatory information received from another member state, the disclosing state shall communicate its intention and purpose for such disclosure to the member state which originally provided that information.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106 Article VII -- Establishment of the Interstate Teacher Mobility Compact Commission.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(1): The interstate compact member states hereby create and establish a joint public agency known as the Interstate Teacher Mobility Compact Commission:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(1)(a): the commission is a joint interstate governmental agency comprised of states that have enacted the Interstate Teacher Mobility Compact; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(1)(b): nothing in this interstate compact shall be construed to be a waiver of sovereign immunity.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(2)(a): Each member state shall have and be limited to one delegate to the commission, who shall be given the title of commissioner.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(2)(b): The commissioner shall be the primary administrative officer of the state licensing authority or their designee.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(2)(c): Any commissioner may be removed or suspended from office as provided by the law of the state from which the commissioner is appointed.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(2)(d): The member state shall fill any vacancy occurring in the commission within 90 days.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(2)(e): Each commissioner shall be entitled to one vote about the promulgation of rules and creation of bylaws and shall otherwise have an opportunity to participate in the business and affairs of the commission. A commissioner shall vote in person or by such other means as provided in the bylaws. The bylaws may provide for commissioners' participation in meetings by telephone or other means of communication.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(2)(f): The commission shall meet at least once during each calendar year. Additional meetings shall be held as set forth in the bylaws.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(2)(g): The commission shall establish by rule a term of office for commissioners.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3): The commission shall have the following powers and duties:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(a): establish a code of ethics for the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(b): establish the fiscal year of the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(c): establish bylaws for the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(d): maintain its financial records in accordance with the bylaws of the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(e): meet and take such actions as are consistent with the provisions of this interstate compact, the bylaws, and rules of the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(f): promulgate uniform rules to implement and administer this interstate compact. The rules shall have the force and effect of law and shall be binding in all member states. In the event the commission exercises its rulemaking authority in a manner that is beyond the scope of the purposes of the compact, or the powers granted hereunder, then such an action by the commission shall be invalid and have no force and effect of law;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(g): bring and prosecute legal proceedings or actions in the name of the commission, provided that the standing of any member state licensing authority to sue or be sued under applicable law shall not be affected;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(h): purchase and maintain insurance and bonds;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(i): borrow, accept, or contract for services of personnel, including, but not limited to, employees of a member state, or an associated nongovernmental organization that is open to membership by all states;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(j): hire employees, elect, or appoint officers, fix compensation, define duties, grant such individuals appropriate authority to carry out the purposes of the compact, and establish the commission's personnel policies and programs relating to conflicts of interest, qualifications of personnel, and other related personnel matters;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(k): lease, purchase, accept appropriate gifts or donations of, or otherwise own, hold, improve, or use, any property, real, personal or mixed, provided that at all times the commission shall avoid any appearance of impropriety;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(l): sell, convey, mortgage, pledge, lease, exchange, abandon, or otherwise dispose of any property real, personal, or mixed;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(m): establish a budget and make expenditures;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(n): borrow money;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(o): appoint committees, including standing committees composed of members and such other interested persons as may be designated in this interstate compact, rules, or bylaws;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(p): provide and receive information from, and cooperate with, law enforcement agencies;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(q): establish and elect an executive committee;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(r): establish and develop a charter for an Executive Information Governance Committee to advise on facilitating exchange of information; use of information, data privacy, and technical support needs, and provide reports as needed;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(s): perform such other functions as may be necessary or appropriate to achieve the purposes of this interstate compact consistent with the state regulation of teacher licensure; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(3)(t): determine whether a state's adopted language is materially different from the model compact language such that the state would not qualify for participation in the compact.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(a): The executive committee of the Interstate Teacher Mobility Compact Commission shall have the power to act on behalf of the commission according to the terms of this interstate compact.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(b): The executive committee shall be composed of eight voting members:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(b)(i): the commission chair, vice chair, and treasurer; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(b)(ii): five members who are elected by the commission from the current membership:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(b)(ii)(A): four voting members representing geographic regions in accordance with commission rules; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(b)(ii)(B): one at large voting member in accordance with commission rules.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(c): The commission may add or remove members of the executive committee as provided in commission rules.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(d): The executive committee shall meet at least once annually.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(e): The executive committee shall have the following duties and responsibilities:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(e)(i): recommend to the entire commission changes to the rules or bylaws, changes to the compact legislation, fees paid by interstate compact member states such as annual dues, and any compact fee charged by the member states on behalf of the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(e)(ii): ensure commission administration services are appropriately provided, contractual or otherwise;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(e)(iii): prepare and recommend the budget;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(e)(iv): maintain financial records on behalf of the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(e)(v): monitor compliance of member states and provide reports to the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(e)(vi): perform other duties as provided in rules or bylaws.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(i): All meetings of the commission shall be open to the public, and public notice of meetings shall be given in accordance with commission bylaws.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(ii): The commission or the executive committee or other committees of the commission may convene in a closed, nonpublic meeting if the commission or executive committee or other committees of the commission must discuss:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(ii)(A): non-compliance of a Member State with its obligations under the compact;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(ii)(B): the employment, compensation, discipline or other matters, practices or procedures related to specific employees or other matters related to the commission's internal personnel practices and procedures;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(ii)(C): current, threatened, or reasonably anticipated litigation;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(ii)(D): negotiation of contracts for the purchase, lease, or sale of goods, services, or real estate;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(ii)(E): accusing any person of a crime or formally censuring any person;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(ii)(F): disclosure of trade secrets or commercial or financial information that is privileged or confidential;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(ii)(G): disclosure of information of a personal nature where disclosure would constitute a clearly unwarranted invasion of personal privacy;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(ii)(H): disclosure of investigative records compiled for law enforcement purposes;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(ii)(I): disclosure of information related to any investigative reports prepared by or on behalf of or for use of the commission or other committee charged with responsibility of investigation or determination of compliance issues pursuant to the compact;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(ii)(J): matters specifically exempted from disclosure by federal or member state statute; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(ii)(K): other matters as set forth by commission bylaws and rules.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(iii): If a meeting, or portion of a meeting, is closed pursuant to this provision, the commission's legal counsel or designee shall certify that the meeting may be closed and shall reference each relevant exempting provision.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(f)(iv): The commission shall keep minutes of commission meetings and shall provide a full and accurate summary of actions taken, and the reasons therefore, including a description of the views expressed. All documents considered in connection with an action shall be identified in such minutes. All minutes and documents of a closed meeting shall remain under seal, subject to release by a majority vote of the commission or order of a court of competent jurisdiction.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(g): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(g)(i): The commission shall pay, or provide for the payment of, the reasonable expenses of its establishment, organization, and ongoing activities.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(g)(ii): The commission may accept all appropriate donations and grants of money, equipment, supplies, materials, and services, and receive, utilize, and dispose of the same, provided that at all times the commission shall avoid any appearance of impropriety or conflict of interest.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(g)(iii): The commission may levy on and collect an annual assessment from each member state or impose fees on other parties to cover the cost of the operations and activities of the commission, in accordance with the commission rules.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(g)(iv): The commission shall not incur obligations of any kind prior to securing the funds adequate to meet the same; nor shall the commission pledge the credit of any of the member states, except by and with the authority of the member state.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(g)(v): The commission shall keep accurate accounts of all receipts and disbursements. The receipts and disbursements of the commission shall be subject to accounting procedures established under commission bylaws. All receipts and disbursements of funds of the commission shall be reviewed annually in accordance with commission bylaws, and a report of the review shall be included in and become part of the annual report of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(h): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(h)(i): The members, officers, executive director, employees and representatives of the commission shall be immune from suit and liability, either personally or in their official capacity, for any claim for damage to or loss of property or personal injury or other civil liability caused by or arising out of any actual or alleged act, error or omission that occurred, or that the person against whom the claim is made had a reasonable basis for believing occurred within the scope of commission employment, duties or responsibilities; provided that nothing in this paragraph shall be construed to protect any such person from suit or liability for any damage, loss, injury, or liability caused by the intentional or willful or wanton misconduct of that person.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(h)(ii): The commission shall defend any member, officer, executive director, employee, or representative of the commission in any civil action seeking to impose liability arising out of any actual or alleged act, error, or omission that occurred within the scope of commission employment, duties, or responsibilities, or that the person against whom the claim is made had a reasonable basis for believing occurred within the scope of commission employment, duties, or responsibilities; provided that nothing herein shall be construed to prohibit that person from retaining his or her own counsel; and provided further, that the actual or alleged act, error, or omission did not result from that person's intentional or willful or wanton misconduct.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1106(4)(h)(iii): The commission shall indemnify and hold harmless any member, officer, executive director, employee, or representative of the commission for the amount of any settlement or judgment obtained against that person arising out of any actual or alleged act, error or omission that occurred within the scope of commission employment, duties, or responsibilities, or that such person had a reasonable basis for believing occurred within the scope of commission employment, duties, or responsibilities, provided that the actual or alleged act, error, or omission did not result from the intentional or willful or wanton misconduct of that person.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1107 Article VIII -- Rulemaking.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1107(1): The commission shall exercise its rulemaking powers pursuant to the criteria set forth in this interstate compact and the rules adopted thereunder. Rules and amendments shall become binding as of the date specified in each rule or amendment.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1107(2): The commission shall promulgate reasonable rules to achieve the intent and purpose of this interstate compact. In the event the commission exercises its rulemaking authority in a manner that is beyond purpose and intent of this interstate compact, or the powers granted hereunder, then such an action by the commission shall be invalid and have no force and effect of law in the member states.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1107(3): If a majority of the legislatures of the member states rejects a rule, by enactment of a statute or resolution in the same manner used to adopt the compact within four years of the date of adoption of the rule, then such rule shall have no further force and effect in any member state.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1107(4): Rules or amendments to the rules shall be adopted or ratified at a regular or special meeting of the commission in accordance with commission rules and bylaws.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1107(5): Upon determination that an emergency exists, the commission may consider and adopt an emergency rule with 48 hours' notice, with opportunity to comment, provided that the usual rulemaking procedures shall be retroactively applied to the rule as soon as reasonably possible, in no event later than ninety days after the effective date of the rule. For the purposes of this provision, an emergency rule is one that must be adopted immediately in order to:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1107(5)(a): meet an imminent threat to public health, safety, or welfare;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1107(5)(b): prevent a loss of Commission or Member State funds;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1107(5)(c): meet a deadline for the promulgation of an administrative rule that is established by federal law or rule; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1107(5)(d): protect public health and safety.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1108 Article IX -- Facilitating information exchange.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1108(1): The commission shall provide for facilitating the exchange of information to administer and implement the provisions of this compact in accordance with the rules of the commission, consistent with generally accepted data protection principles.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1108(2): Nothing in this compact shall be deemed or construed to alter, limit, or inhibit the power of a member state to control and maintain ownership of its licensee information or alter, limit, or inhibit the laws or regulations governing licensee information in the member state.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109 Article X -- Oversight, dispute resolution, and enforcement.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(1)(a): The executive and judicial branches of state government in each member state shall enforce this compact and take all actions necessary and appropriate to effectuate the compact's purposes and intent. The provisions of this compact shall have standing as statutory law.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(1)(b): Venue is proper and judicial proceedings by or against the commission shall be brought solely and exclusively in a court of competent jurisdiction where the principal office of the commission is located. The commission may waive venue and jurisdictional defenses to the extent it adopts or consents to participate in alternative dispute resolution proceedings. Nothing herein shall affect or limit the selection or propriety of venue in any action against a licensee for professional malpractice, misconduct or any such similar matter.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(1)(c): All courts and all administrative agencies shall take judicial notice of the compact, the rules of the commission, and any information provided to a member state pursuant thereto in any judicial or quasijudicial proceeding in a member state pertaining to the subject matter of this compact, or which may affect the powers, responsibilities, or actions of the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(1)(d): The commission shall be entitled to receive service of process in any proceeding regarding the enforcement or interpretation of the compact and shall have standing to intervene in such a proceeding for all purposes. Failure to provide the commission service of process shall render a judgment or order void as to the commission, this compact, or promulgated rules.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(2)(a): If the commission determines that a member state has defaulted in the performance of its obligations or responsibilities under this compact or the promulgated rules, the commission shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(2)(a)(i): provide written notice to the defaulting state and other member states of the nature of the default, the proposed means of curing the default or any other action to be taken by the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(2)(a)(ii): provide remedial training and specific technical assistance regarding the default.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(3): If a state in default fails to cure the default, the defaulting state may be terminated from the compact upon an affirmative vote of a majority of the commissioners of the member states, and all rights, privileges and benefits conferred on that state by this compact may be terminated on the effective date of termination. A cure of the default does not relieve the offending state of obligations or liabilities incurred during the period of default.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(4): Termination of membership in the compact shall be imposed only after all other means of securing compliance have been exhausted. Notice of intent to suspend or terminate shall be given by the commission to the governor, the majority and minority leaders of the defaulting state's legislature, the state licensing authority and each of the member states.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(5): A state that has been terminated is responsible for all assessments, obligations, and liabilities incurred through the effective date of termination, including obligations that extend beyond the effective date of termination.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(6): The commission shall not bear any costs related to a state that is found to be in default or that has been terminated from the compact, unless agreed upon in writing between the commission and the defaulting state.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(7): The defaulting state may appeal the action of the commission by petitioning the U.S. District Court for the District of Columbia or the federal district where the commission has its principal offices. The prevailing party shall be awarded all costs of such litigation, including reasonable attorney fees.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(8): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(8)(a): Upon request by a member state, the commission shall attempt to resolve disputes related to the compact that arise among member states and between member and nonmember states.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(8)(b): The commission shall promulgate a rule providing for both binding and nonbinding alternative dispute resolutions for disputes as appropriate.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(9): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(9)(a): The commission, in the reasonable exercise of its discretion, shall enforce the provisions and rules of this compact.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1109(9)(b): By majority vote, the commission may initiate legal action in the U.S. District Court for the District of Columbia or the federal district where the commission has its principal offices against a member state in default to enforce compliance with the provisions of the compact and its promulgated rules and bylaws. The relief sought may include both injunctive relief and damages. In the event judicial enforcement is necessary, the prevailing party shall be awarded all costs of such litigation, including reasonable attorney fees. The remedies herein shall not be the exclusive remedies of the commission. The commission may pursue any other remedies available under federal or state law.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1110 Article XI -- Effectuation, withdrawal, and amendment.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1110(1): 53E-6-1109; 53E-6-1106(3)(t) The compact shall come into effect on the date on which the compact statute is enacted into law in the tenth member state.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1110(1)(a): On or after the effective date of the compact, the commission shall convene and review the enactment of each of the charter member states to determine if the statute enacted by each such charter member state is materially different from the model compact statute.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1110(1)(b): 53E-6-1109 A charter member state whose enactment is found to be materially different from the model Compact statute shall be entitled to the default process set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1110(1)(c): 53E-6-1106(3)(t) Member states enacting the compact subsequent to the charter member states shall be subject to the process set forth in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1110(2): If any member state is later found to be in default, or is terminated or withdraws from the compact, the commission shall remain in existence and the compact shall remain in effect even if the number of member States should be less than 10.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1110(3): Any state that joins the compact after the commission's initial adoption of the rules and bylaws shall be subject to the rules and bylaws as they exist on the date on which the compact becomes law in that state. Any rule that has been previously adopted by the commission shall have the full force and effect of law on the day the compact becomes law in that state, as the rules and bylaws may be amended as provided in this compact.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1110(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1110(4)(a): Any member state may withdraw from this compact by enacting a statute repealing the same.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1110(4)(b): A member state's withdrawal shall not take effect until six months after enactment of the repealing statute.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1110(4)(c): Withdrawal shall not affect the continuing requirement of the withdrawing state's licensing authority to comply with the investigative and adverse action reporting requirements of this act prior to the effective date of withdrawal.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1110(5): This compact may be amended by the member states. No amendment to this compact shall become effective and binding upon any member state until it is enacted into the laws of all member states.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1111 Article XII -- Construction and severability.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1111(1): This compact shall be liberally construed to effectuate the purposes thereof.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1111(2): The provisions of this compact shall be severable and if any phrase, clause, sentence, or provision of this compact is declared to be contrary to the constitution of any member state or a state seeking membership in the compact, or of the United States or the applicability thereof to any other government, agency, person or circumstance is held invalid, the validity of the remainder of this compact and the applicability thereof to any government, agency, person, or circumstance shall not be affected thereby.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1111(3): If this compact shall be held contrary to the constitution of any member state, the compact shall remain in full force and effect as to the remaining member states and in full force and effect as to the member state affected as to all severable matters.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1112 Article XIII -- Consistent effect and conflict with other state laws.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1112(1): Nothing herein shall prevent or inhibit the enforcement of any other law of a member state that is not inconsistent with the compact.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1112(2): Any laws, statutes, regulations, or other legal requirements in a member state in conflict with the compact are superseded to the extent of the conflict.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-6-1112(3): All permissible agreements between the commission and the member states are binding in accordance with their terms.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 53E - Chapter 7 - Special Education
***************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as "Special Education."

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(1): "Child with a disability" means the same as that term is defined in 34 C.F.R. Sec. 300.308.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(2): "Due process hearing" means an administrative due process hearing authorized by 20 U.S.C. Sec. 1415.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(3): "IEP team" means the same as that term is defined in 34 C.F.R. Sec. 300.321.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(4): "LEA special education program" means systems an LEA establishes to:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(4)(a): implement an eligible student's IEP;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(4)(b): appropriately and timely identify eligible students;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(4)(c): evaluate and classify eligible students by qualified personnel;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(4)(d): implement standards for special education classes and services;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(4)(e): deliver special education service responsibilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(4)(f): ensure special education instructional staff are appropriately credentialed; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(4)(g): provide services for dual enrollment students that are:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(4)(g)(i): eligible students; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(4)(g)(ii): attending public school on a part-time basis.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(5): "Least restrictive environment" means the same as that term is defined in 34 C.F.R. Secs. 300.114 through 300.116.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(6): "Special education" means the same as that term is defined in 34 C.F.R. Sec. 300.39.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(7): "Specially designed instruction" means the same as that term is defined in 34 C.F.R. Sec. 300.39.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(8): "Student who is eligible for special education services" or "eligible student" means a child with a disability who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(8)(a): at least 3 years old but younger than 22 years old; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-201(8)(b): 22 years old, if the school year in which the child with a disability turned 22 years old has not yet ended.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-202 Free appropriate public education for eligible students.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
An eligible student who has not received a regular high school diploma is entitled to a free appropriate public education.

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-204 State board special education authority and duties -- Rulemaking.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-204(1): The state board shall have general control and supervision over LEA special education programs in the state for eligible students.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-204(2): (1) A program described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-204(3): 53G-6-702 In accordance with federal and state law, the state board shall make rules to implement this part, including provisions that ensure:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-204(3)(a): appropriate and timely identification of a potentially eligible student;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-204(3)(b): the evaluation of a student and classification of a student as an eligible student by qualified personnel;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-204(3)(c): standards for special education services and supports;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-204(3)(d): availability of LEA special education programs;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-204(3)(e): delivery of special education in the least restrictive environment as determined by an eligible student's IEP team;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-204(3)(f): certification and qualification for the instructional staff of eligible students; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-204(3)(g): 53G-6-702 special education services for eligible students who are dual enrollment students attending public school on a part-time basis as described in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-204(4): (1) In accordance with federal and state law, the state board may make rules to otherwise administer the state board's authority described in Subsection

----------------------------------------------------------
In accordance with

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-207(3): (3); (3); (3); (3)

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-207(3)(b): (3); (3); (3); (3)

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208 Special education dispute resolution -- Rulemaking -- Due process hearing -- Right to appeal.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(1): (1)(a) In accordance with this section, the state board shall make rules that:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(1)(a): allow for a prompt, fair, and final resolution of a dispute that arises over the provision of special education to an eligible student;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(1)(b): establish and maintain procedural safeguards that meet the requirements of 20 U.S.C. Sec. 1415; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(1)(c): (1)(a) establish timelines that provide adequate time to address and resolve a dispute described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(2): (1)(a) A party to a dispute described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(3): (2); (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(3)(a): (2) If a dispute is not resolved informally as described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(3)(b): (2) Upon request of a party to a dispute described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(3)(b)(i): conduct a due process hearing; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(3)(b)(ii): issue a decision on the due process hearing.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(4)(a): A party to a due process hearing may appeal the decision resulting from the due process hearing by filing a civil action with a court described in 20 U.S.C. Sec. 1415(i), if the party files the action within 30 days after the day on which the due process hearing decision was issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-208(4)(b): If parties to a due process hearing fail to reach agreement on the payment of attorney fees for the due process hearing, a party may seek to recover attorney fees in accordance with 20 U.S.C. Sec. 1415(i) by filing a court action within 30 days after the day on which the due process hearing decision was issued.

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-209(1)(c): employ staff who are trained and supervised by appropriately credentialed staff necessary to provide specially designed instruction and related services.

"I acknowledge that:Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-405(1): 59-7-625; 59-10-1041 A person that makes a donation to a scholarship granting organization to help fund scholarships through the program may be eligible to receive a nonrefundable tax credit as described in Sections

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-405(5)(c): Upon acceptance of a scholarship, the parent assumes full financial responsibility for the education of the scholarship recipient.

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-405(5)(e): The creation of the program or granting of a scholarship does not:

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-406 Private school regulation -- Student records.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-406(1): Nothing in this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-406(1)(a): grants additional authority to any state agency or LEA to regulate private schools except as expressly described in this part; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-406(1)(b): expands the regulatory authority of the state, a state office holder, or a local school district to impose any additional regulation of a qualifying school beyond those necessary to enforce the requirements of the program.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-406(2): A qualifying school shall be given the maximum freedom to provide for the educational needs of a scholarship recipient who attends the qualifying school without unlawful governmental control.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-406(3): 53E-7-403 Except as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-406(4): Title 53E, Chapter 9, Student Privacy and Data Protection A local education agency or school in a local education agency in which a scholarship recipient was previously enrolled shall provide to a qualifying school in which the scholarship recipient is currently enrolled a copy of all requested school records relating to the scholarship recipient, subject to:

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-406(4)(b): Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act, 20 U.S.C. Sec. 1232g.

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408 Eligible private schools.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1): (1)(f)(i); (1)(g); 53G-11-402; Chapter 6, Education Professional Licensure To be eligible to enroll a scholarship student, a private school shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(a): have a physical location in Utah where the scholarship students attend classes and have direct contact with the school's teachers;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(b)(i): contract with an independent licensed certified public accountant to conduct an Agreed Upon Procedures engagement as adopted by the state board, or obtain an audit and report from a licensed independent certified public accountant that conforms with the following requirements:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(b)(i)(A): the audit shall be performed in accordance with generally accepted auditing standards;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(b)(i)(B): the financial statements shall be presented in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(b)(i)(C): the audited financial statements shall be as of a period within the last 12 months; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(b)(ii): submit the audit report or report of the agreed upon procedure to the state board when the private school applies to accept scholarship students;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(c): comply with the antidiscrimination provisions of 42 U.S.C. 2000d;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(d): meet state and local health and safety laws and codes;

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(e)(i): the special education services that will be provided to the student, including the cost of those services;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(e)(ii): tuition costs;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(e)(iii): additional fees a parent will be required to pay during the school year; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(e)(iv): the skill or grade level of the curriculum in which the prospective student will participate;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(f): (1)(f)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(f)(i): administer an annual assessment of each scholarship student's academic progress; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(f)(ii): (1)(f)(i) report the results of the assessment described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(g): employ or contract with teachers who:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(g)(i): hold baccalaureate or higher degrees;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(g)(ii): have at least three years of teaching experience in public or private schools; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(g)(iii): have the necessary skills, knowledge, or expertise that qualifies the teacher to provide instruction:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(g)(iii)(A): in the subject or subjects taught; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(g)(iii)(B): to the special needs students taught;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(h): (1)(g) maintain documentation demonstrating that teachers at the private school meet the qualifications described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(i): 53G-11-402; Chapter 6, Education Professional Licensure require the following individuals to submit to a nationwide, fingerprint-based criminal background check and ongoing monitoring, in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(i)(i): Chapter 6, Education Professional Licensure an employee who does not hold a current Utah educator license issued by the state board under
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(i)(ii): a contract employee; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(i)(iii): a volunteer who is given significant unsupervised access to a student in connection with the volunteer's assignment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(1)(j): provide to the parent of a scholarship student the relevant credentials of the teachers who will be teaching the scholarship student.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-7-408(2): (1)(b); (1)(b); (1)(b) A private school is not eligible to enroll scholarship students if:

Utah Code Annotated - Title 53E - Chapter 8 - Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind
*************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as "Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind."

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(1): "Advisory council" means the Advisory Council for the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(2): "Alternate format" includes braille, audio, digital text, or large print.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(3): "Associate superintendent" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(3)(a): the associate superintendent of the Utah School for the Deaf; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(3)(b): the associate superintendent of the Utah School for the Blind.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(4): "Blind" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(4)(a): if the person is three years of age or older but younger than 22 years of age, having a visual impairment that, even with correction, adversely affects educational performance or substantially limits one or more major life activities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(4)(b): if the person is younger than three years of age, having a visual impairment.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(5): "Blindness" means an impairment in vision in which central visual acuity:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(5)(a): does not exceed 20/200 in the better eye with correcting lenses; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(5)(b): is accompanied by a limit to the field of vision in the better eye to such a degree that its widest diameter subtends an angle of no greater than 20 degrees.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(6): "Cortical visual impairment" means a cortical or cerebral visual impairment:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(6)(a): that:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(6)(a)(i): affects the visual cortex or visual tracts of the brain;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(6)(a)(ii): is caused by damage to the visual pathways to the brain;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(6)(a)(iii): affects a person's visual discrimination, acuity, processing, and interpretation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(6)(a)(iv): is often present in conjunction with other disabilities or eye conditions that cause visual impairment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(6)(b): in which the eyes and optic nerves of the affected person appear normal and the person's pupil responses are normal.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(7): "Deaf" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(7)(a): if the person is three years of age or older but younger than 22 years of age, having hearing loss, whether permanent or fluctuating, that, even with amplification, adversely affects educational performance or substantially limits one or more major life activities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(7)(b): if the person is younger than three years of age, having hearing loss.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(8): 53E-8-401 "Deafblind" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(8)(a): if the person is three years of age or older but younger than 22 years of age:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(8)(a)(i): deaf;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(8)(a)(ii): blind; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(8)(a)(iii): having hearing loss and visual impairments that cause such severe communication and other developmental and educational needs that the person cannot be accommodated in special education programs solely for students who are deaf or blind; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(8)(b): 53E-8-401 if the person is younger than three years of age, having both hearing loss and vision impairments that are diagnosed as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(9): "Deafness" means a hearing loss so severe that the person is impaired in processing linguistic information through hearing, with or without amplification.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(10): 53E-6-201 "Educator" means an individual who is:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(10)(a): 53E-6-201 licensed by the state board under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(10)(b): credentialed by the governing body of the individual's area of professional practice.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(11): "Functional blindness" means a disorder in which the physical structures of the eye may be functioning, but the person does not attend to, examine, utilize, or accurately process visual information.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(12): "Functional hearing loss" means a central nervous system impairment that results in abnormal auditory perception, including an auditory processing disorder or auditory neuropathy/dys-synchrony, in which parts of the auditory system may be functioning, but the person does not attend to, respond to, localize, utilize, or accurately process auditory information.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(13): "Hard of hearing" means having a hearing loss, excluding deafness.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(14): "Individualized education program" or "IEP" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(14)(a): a written statement for a student with a disability that is developed, reviewed, and revised in accordance with the Individuals with Disabilities Education Act, 20 U.S.C. Sec. 1400 et seq.; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(14)(b): an individualized family service plan developed:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(14)(b)(i): for a child with a disability who is younger than three years of age; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(14)(b)(ii): in accordance with the Individuals with Disabilities Education Act, 20 U.S.C. Sec. 1400 et seq.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(15): "LEA" means a local education agency that has administrative control and direction for public education.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(16): 53G-6-302 "LEA of record" means the school district of residence of a student as determined under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(17): "Low vision" means an impairment in vision in which:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(17)(a): visual acuity is at 20/70 or worse;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(17)(b): the visual field is reduced to less than 20 degrees;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(17)(c): even with correction, educational performance is affected; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(17)(d): at least one major life activity is substantially limited.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(18): "Parent Infant Program" means a program at the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind that provides services:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(18)(a): through an interagency agreement with the Department of Health to children younger than three years of age who are deaf, blind, or deafblind; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(18)(b): to children younger than three years of age who are deafblind through Deafblind Services of the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(19): "Section 504" means Section 504 of the Rehabilitation Act of 1973.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(20): "Superintendent" means the superintendent of the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-102(21): "Visual impairment" includes partial sightedness, low vision, blindness, cortical visual impairment, functional blindness, and degenerative conditions that lead to blindness or severe loss of vision.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-201 Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind created -- Designated LEA -- Services statewide.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-201(1): The Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind is created as a single public school agency that includes:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-201(1)(a): the Utah School for the Deaf;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-201(1)(b): the Utah School for the Blind;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-201(1)(c): programs for students who are deafblind; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-201(1)(d): the Parent Infant Program.

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-201(2)(a): 53E-8-401 may provide services to students statewide:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-201(2)(a)(i): who are deaf, blind, or deafblind; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-201(2)(a)(ii): 53E-8-401 who are neither deaf, blind, nor deafblind, if allowed under rules of the state board established pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-201(2)(b): shall serve as the designated LEA for a student and assume the responsibilities of providing services as prescribed through the student's IEP or Section 504 accommodation plan when the team that develops the student's IEP or Section 504 accommodation plan determines that the student be placed at the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-201(3): When the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind becomes a student's designated LEA, the LEA of record and the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind shall ensure that all rights and requirements regarding individual student assessment, eligibility, services, placement, and procedural safeguards provided through the Individuals with Disabilities Education Act, 20 U.S.C. Sec. 1400 et seq. and Section 504 of the Rehabilitation Act of 1973, as amended, remain in force.

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401 Eligibility for services of the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind.

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(1): (3); (4); (5) Except as provided in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(1)(a): a resident of Utah;

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(1)(d): identified as deaf, blind, or deafblind through:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(1)(d)(i): the special education eligibility determination process; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(1)(d)(ii): the Section 504 eligibility determination process.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(2)(a): In determining eligibility for an individual who is younger than age three and is deafblind, the following information may be used:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(2)(a)(i): opthalmological and audiological documentation;
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(2)(a)(ii): functional vision or hearing assessments and evaluations; or
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(2)(a)(iii): informed clinical opinion conducted by a person with expertise in deafness, blindness, or deafblindness.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(2)(b): Informed clinical opinion shall be:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(2)(b)(i): included in the determination of eligibility when documentation is incomplete or not conclusive; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(2)(b)(ii): based on pertinent records related to the individual's current health status and medical history, an evaluation and observations of the individual's level of sensory functioning, and the needs of the family.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(3)(a): A student who qualifies for special education shall have services and placement determinations made through the IEP process.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(3)(b): A student who qualifies for accommodations under Section 504 shall have services and placement determinations made through the Section 504 team process.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(4): (6)

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-401(6)(b): may make rules to allow a resident of Utah who is neither deaf, blind, nor deafblind to receive services of the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind if the resident is younger than 22 years of age.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-402 Entrance policies and procedures.
-----------------------------------------------------------------
With input from the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind, school districts, parents, and the advisory council, the state board shall establish entrance policies and procedures that IEP teams and Section 504 teams are to consider in making placement recommendations at the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind.

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-403 Educational programs.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-403(1): The Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind shall provide an educational program for a student:
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-403(1)(a): based on assessments of the student's abilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-403(1)(b): in accordance with the student's IEP or Section 504 accommodation plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-403(2): If a student's ability to access the core curriculum is impaired primarily due to a severe sensory loss and requires intensive sensory-based instruction or services, the Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind shall provide an educational program that will enable the student, with accommodations, to access the core curriculum.
Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-403(3): The Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind shall provide instruction in Braille to students who are blind.


Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-404 Administration of statewide assessments.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
The Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind shall annually administer, as applicable, the statewide assessments described in Section

Utah Code Annotated § 53E-8-405 Collaboration with Department of Health and Human Services.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The Utah Schools for the Deaf and the Blind shall collaborate with the Department of Health and Human Services to provide services to children with disabilities who are younger than three years old in accordance with the Individuals with Disabilities Education Act, 20 U.S.C. Sec. 1400 et seq.
